first you need some home-made chicken stock [step] don't use store bought powder , it's not hard to make - i promise you this as a former kitchen assassin turned food-lover ! [step] to make stock: [step] bring 3 l of water to a boil in a 4-6 l pot [step] add the chicken frames , a good dash of salt and the bay leaves [step] you will add more salt later but this helps to extract the maximum flavor from the chicken [step] reduce heat to simmer for 1 hour covered , skimming occasionally [step] do not simmer for too much longer than this or the bones start to decalcify and make the stock bitter flavoured [step] in the meantime: [step] clean and rough chop 2 [step] 5 kg of potatos , set aside [step] clean and rough chop 1 large leek , set aside [step] you're going to puree it all once it's nice and soft from cooking so don't obsess over getting perfect , small diced cubes you just want it chopped up enough so that they'll cook out nicely in the pot [step] back to the stock: your hour of simmering is done and voila -- you have stock ! [step] now remove the chicken frames , set aside [step] strain the stock so that you catch any fine bones that may have come loose while simmering [step] add the leek [step] add the potato [step] boil till soft [step] once the chicken frames are cool to a temperature you can handle them , chip whatever meat there is off [step] set the meat aside [step] pluck out the bay leaves [step] whiz soup till smooth [step] we use a bar mixer personally [step] return chicken meat to pot [step] add salt and pepper to taste - for those who aren't familiar , this means add a bit , stir it well , let the flavors mingle for a minute or two , spoon a bit out and taste to tell if it suits your preferences [step] don't be afraid of the salt -- one of the basic tenants of cheffing is that salt equals flavor [step] soup is now ready to eat but if you prefer a thicker soup , allow to simmer uncovered to reduce , till it's as thick as you like [end]	hey nic add the chicken  leek and potato soup

[step] i rinse them in the strainer with hot water- be prepared , they don't smell good at all ! i sprinkle them with a few teaspoons of lemon juice and let them sit a minute , then rinse again in hot water [step] let them drain well- water is our enemy in this recipe ! [step] next , get out a big frying pan- you don't need any grease or anything the noodles don't tend to burn or brownand they don't stick [step] dump the noodles in the pan and over high heat start cooking them [step] i stirred mine around a lot- [step] as you stir and they start to dry , they start making a "squeaking" kind of noise as you push them [step] i kept mine on the heat until they lost translucency and bits and parts seemed a bit "shriveled" [step] take them off the heat [step] i know , at this point it doesn't look like much does it ? don't worry if you over cook , it will just mean 1 or 2 less cookies [step] if you undercook it just means your cookie dough maybe a little runny , and you may need another teaspoon of coco powder to "thicken" it [step] after they have cooled for a few minutes i put them in my handy mini ninja food processor [step] i ran it until it almost looked like a gel- [step] then i threw in the honey , coco powder , baking powder , saltand processed it quickly till blended [step] it seemed a hair on the runny side , so i threw it in the fridge for an hour and hoped for the best- [step] here is what it looked like after being in the fridge- [step] i covered a cookie sheet with a piece of tin and sprayed with pam non stick cooking spray [step] i tried 5 minutes at 375- but the tops were clearly sticky / raw still [step] so 10 minutes [step] i was thrilled with what i had created ! [step] sara was my brave , brave guinea pig [step] she topped hers with a touch of sugar free cool whip- i watched her face carefully , mostly to know if i was going to need to duck if she spit it back out- but she declared them a success ! she said her first thought was it was a lot like the flourless chocolate torte in flavor 3 hours later i broke one a part and they are just as moist as can be [step] truly a miracle cookie [end]	10 calorie chocolate miracle noodle cookies

filling: mix all ingredients , beating well until smooth [step] cover and refrigerate to cool for 1 hour or overnight [step] crepes: to a large pyrex measuring cup or a bowl , and using a hand mixer , add all crepe ingredients and mix well until it coats the spoons with a thin film [step] cover and refrigerate for 1 hour [step] using a large nonstick pan , spray with oil , and heat the pan over medium-high heat [step] stir the batter again , and pour about 1 / 3 cup of batter into the pan , swirling the pan to coat and thin out the crepe [step] when the crepes pull away from the edge of the pan in about 30 seconds , remove from the heat and run a spatula across the edge of the pan to release the crepe [step] slide the crepe onto a sheet of parchment paper [step] carefully lift the crepe and flip over into the pan to cook the other side [step] slide the crepe onto a parchment paper , this time covering with another sheet so there will be parchment between each crepe [step] repeat for remaining crepes , stirring the batter at brief intervals to re-suspend the ingredients [step] assembly: while remaining stacked , spoon about 1 / 4 cup of the chilled filling onto the center of the first crepe [step] fold two opposite sides of the crepe over the filling until they almost meet and then fold over the opposite sides to seal [step] set finished 'eggroll or burrito' shaped blintz aside on the parchment paper with the seam side down [step] repeat for remaining blintzes [step] cook: melt about 1 tablespoon of butter in the skillet over medium heat , beginning with the seam side down [step] saute blintzes 2-3 minutes per side , until golden brown [step] flip the blintzes carefully so as not to break break them up or allow the cheese to escape [step] do in batches , adding more butter as needed [step] serve with a dollop of sour cream and a dusting of powdered sugar [end]	2bleu s cheese blintzes

first layer - mix all ingredients together to form a crumbly mixture [step] press into the bottom of a 9 x 13" pan , pressing firmly [step] place pan in the freezer to set while preparing the next layer [step] second layer - mix the first three ingredients together , using enough milk to make a stiff , frosting-like consistency [step] if desired , add a drop of yellow food coloring [step] do not add too much milk , you want the mixture to be pretty stiff , but still spreadable [step] remove the pan from the freezer and scrape the second layer onto the first , spreading as evenly as possible , and then using your hands to press down to smooth [step] return pan to freezer [step] third layer - melt the chocolate chips together with the butter [step] you can use a double boiler , but i have had good luck using a small saucepan and very low heat , with stirring [step] remove the pan from the freezer [step] pour the melted chocolate mixture over the second layer [step] working quickly , spread the chocolate layer evenly [step] return the pan to the freezer for no more than a few minutes [step] you want the chocolate to begin to set before you cut the bars but if you wait too long , the chocolate will be too hard and you won't be able to cut through it without it breaking [step] the point at which the chocolate loses its shine and takes on a dull appearance is the right time to remove the pan from the freezer and cut into small squares [step] after cutting , return to the freezer to harden completely , then remove from the pan [step] store in the refrigerator [end]	3 layer bars

do not boil ribs , but cut away any large amounts of silver skin or some of the fat [step] generously season both sides of the ribs with salt , pepper and season-all [step] line a cookie sheet with heavy duty foil [step] spray foil with cooking spray lightly [step] put ribs in 350 degree oven for approximately 20 minutes , until meat starts to brown on both sides , flipping as needed [step] brush on your favorite bbq sauce and put back in the 350 degree oven until bbq sauce starts to caramelize but not burn , approximately 20 minutes [step] flip them half way through [step] once sauce is caramelized and cooked into the meat add another good amount of sauce to the tops of the ribs [step] try not to let too much sauce fall to the foil , but it's okay if some gets on it [step] with top of ribs facing up , cover with a low-tented aluminum foil and seal all sides tightly by curling foil under the lip or under the cookie sheet itself [step] the goal is to not let the steam out as it cooks [step] turn oven down to 250 degrees ! very important or the sauce will burn ! [step] put ribs back in at 250 degrees and set a timer for approx 2 hours [step] take cookie sheet out and pull back one corner of the foil [step] poke a fork at one of the ribs -- the meat should easily come off the bone [step] if it doesn't , put back in the 250 degree oven and check every 20 minutes or so to see if the steam worked its magic [step] i've done two full sheets of ribs for a total of 4 long slabs of baby back ribs in around 4 hours total cooking time [step] you will not believe how easy and tasty these are ! once the browning part is over you basically forget about them [step] there's really no wrong way to season them or sauce them [step] serve with your favorite sides and enjoy ! crush the rennet into the water and stir to dissolve [step] pour milk into a non-reactive pot [step] place over medium heat [step] sprinkle the citric acid over the milk and stir a few times [step] heat milk to 88f [step] milk will begin to curdle [step] at 88f , add the rennet solution and continue stirring slowly every few minutes until the milk reaches 105f turn off the heat [step] large curds will appear and begin to separate from the whey [step] with a slotted spoon or mesh strainer , scoop the curd into a large glass bowl [step] press the curds gently with your hand and pour off as much whey as possible [step] microwave curds on high for 1 minute , then drain off all the excess whey [step] with a spoon , press curds into a ball until cool [step] microwave two more times for 35 seconds each , and continue to drain the whey and work cheese into a ball [step] in the meantime , place the whey over medium heat and let it heat to about 175f [step] when cheese is cool enough to touch , knead it like bread dough until smooth [step] when you can stretch it like taffy , it is done [step] you can sprinkle 1 to 2 teaspoons salt into the cheese while kneading and stretching it [step] the cheese will become stretchy , smooth and shiny [step] if it is difficult to stretch and breaks easily , dip it into the hot whey for a few seconds to make it warm and pliable [step] then pick it up again and stretch it into a long rope [step] fold over and stretch again [step] dip in hot whey as needed to make the cheese pliable [step] when the cheese is smooth and shiny , it is ready to eat [step] shape it into a log or golf-size balls , then store in a solution of 2 teaspoons salt to 1 cup water [end]	30 minute fresh mozzarella cheese homemade

preheat the oven to 350f [step] bring a tea kettle of water to a boil [step] make the caramel: have ready a 9-inch glass pie plate and a pair of potholders or oven mitts [step] pour the sugar into a small , heavy saucepan [step] set it over medium-low heat until the sugar starts to liquefy and form clumps [step] stir slowly and constantly [step] the sugar will eventually liquefy completely , then begin to color [step] pay careful attention to the caramel at this point [step] once it starts to color it will darken quickly [step] pull the pan from the heat when the caramel is the color of a bright , shiny penny [step] scrape all the caramel into the pie plate , put on the mitts and grab the pie plate firmly [step] carefully but quickly rotate so the bottom and halfway up the sides of the plate are coated with caramel [step] set the prepared pan into a shallow roasting pan [step] make the filling: combine the evaporated milk , condensed milk , milk , eggs , yolks , and vanilla in a blender jar [step] blend on very low speed just until the eggs are blended , a few seconds [step] add the media crema and blend a few seconds until smooth [step] let stand for a minute then scoop off any foam that rises to the surface [step] put the roasting pan with the caramel-lined pie plate in the oven [step] pour the custard mix into the pie plate [step] carefully pour enough water from the tea kettle into the roasting pan to come halfway up the side of the pie plate [step] bake until the center of the flan is set , about 35 minutes [step] remove from the oven and cool to room temperature in the water bath [step] refrigerate until completely chilled , at least 2 hours or up to 1 day [step] to serve , center a large plate over the flan and , with one quick flip invert the flan over the plate [step] give it a few secondsthe flan will slip right out of the mold and onto the plate [step] scrape any caramel left in the mold over the flan [step] serve chilled [step] be extremely careful when working with caramel: by the time the caramel is brown enough to pour into the mold it will be very hotmuch hotter than boiling water [step] handle the pot and pie plate carefully and , when tilting the pan , keep it at arms length from you [end]	4 milk mexican flan

preparing dough for storage: [step] warm the water slightly [step] it should feel just a little warmer than body temperature [step] warm water will rise the dough to the right point for storage in about 2 hours [step] with cold water it will need 3-4 hours [step] add the yeast to the water in a 5 quart bowl or , preferably , in a resealable , lidded plastic food container or food-grade bucket [step] don't worry about getting it all to dissolve [step] mix in the flour and salt - kneading is unnecessary [step] add all of the flour at once , measuring it in with dry-ingredient measuring cups , by gently scooping up the flour , then sweeping the top level with a knife or spatula [step] don't press down into the flour as you scoop or you'll throw off the measurement [step] mix with a wooden spoon , a high-capacity food processor fitted with the dough attachment , or a heavy duty stand mixer fitted with the dough hook until the mixture is uniform [step] if you're hand mixing and it becomes too difficult to incorporate all the flour with the spoon , you can reach into your mixing vessel with very wet hands and press the mixture together [step] don't knead , it isn't necessary [step] you're finished when everything is uniformly moist , without dry patches [step] it takes a few minutes , and will yield a dough that is wet and loose enough to conform to the shape of its container [step] allow to rise [step] cover with lid [step] allow the mixture to rise at room temperature until it begins to collapse , approx 2 hours , depending on room temperature , and initial water temperature longer rising times , up to 5 hours , won't harm the result [step] you can use a portion of the dough any time after this period [step] fully refrigerated dough is less sticky and easier to work with than dough at room temperature [step] on baking day: [step] prepare your loaf tin , tray , or whatever you're baking it in / on [step] sprinkle the surface of your refrigerated dough with four [step] pull up and cut of a grapefruit-size piece of dough , using a serrated knife [step] hold the mass of dough in your hands and add a little more flour as needed so it won't stick to your hands [step] gently stretch the surface of the dough around to the bottom on all 4 sides , rotating the ball a quarter-turn as you go [step] most of the dusting flour will fall off - that's fine , it isn't meant to be incorporated [step] the bottom of the loaf may appear to be a collection of bunched ends , but it will sort itself out during resting and baking [step] the correctly shaped final product will be smooth and cohesive [step] the entire process should take no more than 30 - 60 seconds [step] rest the loaf and let it rise in the form , on the tray / pizza peel , for about 40 minutes depending on the age of the dough , you may not see much rise during this period [step] that's fine , more rising will occur during baking [step] twenty minutes before baking , preheat the oven to 450f place an empty broiler tray for holding water on any other shelf that won't interfere with the rising bread [step] dust and slash [step] dust the top of the loaf liberally with flour , which will allow the slashing knife to pass without sticking [step] slash a quarter inch deep cross , diagonal lines , or tic-tac-toe pattern on top using a serrated knife [step] after a 20 min preheat you're ready to bake , even though the oven thermometer won't be at full temperature yet [step] put your loaf in the oven [step] pour about 1 cup of hot water into the broiler tray and close the oven to trap the steam [step] bake for about 30 minutes , or until the crust is nicely browned and firm to the touch [step] store the rest of the dough in the fridge in your lidded container and use it over the next 14 days [step] the flavour and texture improves , becoming like sourdough [step] even 24 hours of storage improves the flavour [step] this is the standard bread [step] there are loads of variations - both savory and sweet - in the book [end]	5 minute artisan bread
